		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColor.exposed_params.g_vColor0:name_ref"		"Base Coat"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColor.exposed_params.g_vColor0:shorthelp"		"A base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColor.exposed_params.g_vColor0:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			b {
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			</body>
			</html>"

The roughness map allows you to define the condition and character of a surface. This can be used to make your finish look distressed and weathered or like it has a fresh coat of paint.</p>

		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColor.exposed_params.g_tPaintByNumberMasks:shorthelp"		"The red channel masks the painted area."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColor.exposed_params.g_tPaintByNumberMasks:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<p>All finishable weapons are divided into regions that define how the finish styles apply their colors and patterns. Paint by number masks control which areas can be anodized or given a patina, and where patterns and accent colors appear.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/paintbynumber.png' />
			<br>
			<p>There are also predefined areas on each weapon that don’t get refinished, such as shell casings, the inside of barrels, firing rods, etc.
			<br><br>
			The best way to visualize the paint by number areas on a weapon is to load it up in the Counter-Strike 2 Workshop Item Editor and assign some colors.</p>
			</body>
			</html>"

		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColor.econ_instance.g_flWearAmount:name_ref"		"Wear Range"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColor.econ_instance.g_flWearAmount:shorthelp"		"Range of wear values that can be applied to this finish.<br>
			<br>
			On application, random values are chosen within this range so that each application is unique."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColor.econ_instance.g_flWearAmount:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h3 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<p>In general, finishes should be available in all wear values from Factory New to Battle Scarred with a few exceptions. That said the wear values don't have to be the full range and many weapon finishes ship with wear values from Factory New (0.0) to Battle Scarred (0.6).</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/wear.png' />
			<center>On application, random values are chosen within this range so that each application is unique.</center>
			<br>
			<h3>Wear Value Ranges</h3>
			<ul type=circle>
			<li>Factory New:	0.00 - 0.07</li>
			<li>Minimal Wear:	0.07 - 0.15</li>
			<li>Field Tested:	0.15 - 0.37</li>
			<li>Well Worn:		0.37 - 0.44</li>
			<li>Battle Scarred:	0.44 - 1.0</li>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_HydroGraphic.exposed_params.g_tPattern:name_ref"		"Pattern Mask"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_HydroGraphic.exposed_params.g_tPattern:shorthelp"		"Seamless texture utilizing the red, green and blue channels to create three color masks."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_HydroGraphic.exposed_params.g_tPattern:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			.important {
			  color: #eaad3d;
			  font-size: 9pt;
			  white-space: pre-wrap;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>How to Create a Pattern</h2>
			<p>Color images are typically stored in red, green and blue channels that combine additively to represent a large range of color values. For our patterns, we take advantage of this configuration to store three separate images. The final result is a bit bright, but don’t worry, what it looks like here isn’t how it’ll look on a weapon.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_b.png' /><br>
			<span class=important><b><u>IMPORTANT!</u></b> Copy the opacity of each layer into the RGB channels of a new image. The base coat is not included.</span><br>
			<h2>Pattern Application Method</h2>
			<p>Hydrographic finishes are UV mapped, the pattern tiles over the weapon’s existing UVs. To relate that to a real-world application, imagine disassembling the weapon into parts before applying the finish.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/uv_map.png' />
			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			<h2>Durability and Masking</h2>
			<p>On top of their RGB channels, Color textures have an additional, optional “alpha” channel. Hydrographic finishes allow paint masking and durability to be specified in the alpha channel.</p>
			<ul>
			<li>Values around 196 in the alpha channel subtract from the refinishable areas of the weapon.</li>
			<li>Both 128 and 255 have no effect, so the finish wears using the default behavior in these areas.</li>
			<li>Values below 128 increase the durability of the finish. The darker the value, the more durable the paint.</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/durability_hy.png' /><br>
			<p>Each finishable weapon uses a special texture to determine what parts should receive finish. This texture also influences how quickly the finish wears off different features of the weapon. The original, unfinished material underneath is called the substrate.</p>
			<br><br>
			<em>
			<u>When to use a pattern’s alpha channel:</u>
			<ul>
			<li>Your design requires more coverage than the default</li>
			<li>Your design requires more of the substrate to be revealed</li>
			<li>Important features of your design wear too quickly</li>
			<li>Important features of your design should never wear to the substrate</li>
			</em>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_HydroGraphic.exposed_params.g_flPatternTexCoordScale:name_ref"		"Texture Scale"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_HydroGraphic.exposed_params.g_flPatternTexCoordScale:shorthelp"		"Controls size of the texture when applied to a weapon. Increasing the scale repeats the pattern."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_HydroGraphic.exposed_params.g_flPatternTexCoordScale:help"		"			<html>

			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<p>Controls size of the texture when applied to a weapon. Increasing the scale repeats the pattern.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_a.png' />
			<p>Since the weapons are all different sizes, a paint on a large weapon will have correspondingly large features and a paint on a small weapon will have very tiny features. We fix this by further modifying the scale per-weapon. For most styles the scale of the pattern is relative to a pattern sheet size of 36 inches. For styles that use triplanar mapping, 18 inches.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_b.png' />
			<p>Enable \"Ignore Weapon Size Scale\" when the automatic scale adjustment per-weapon is not desired</p>
			</body>
			</html>"

		"Attribute.PaintKit_HydroGraphic.exposed_params.g_vColor0:shorthelp"		"A base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_HydroGraphic.exposed_params.g_vColor0:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;

			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Experiment with color harmonies</h2>
			<p>The same pattern can be reused with different colors to create a new finish.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_c.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"

		"Attribute.PaintKit_HydroGraphic.exposed_params.g_tPaintRoughness:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<p>A greyscale texture that defines the microfacet roughness of the surface. Black is perfectly smooth and white is perfectly rough. The roughness map allows you to define the condition and character of a surface. This can be used to make your finish look distressed and weathered or like it has a fresh coat of paint.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/roughness.png' />
			<p>You can also use a <a href='helpsystem:Attribute.PaintKit_HydroGraphic.exposed_params.g_tNormal'>Normal map</a> to derive surface details that should be represented in the roughness map.</p>

		"Attribute.PaintKit_SprayPaint.exposed_params.g_tPattern:name_ref"		"Pattern Mask"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SprayPaint.exposed_params.g_tPattern:shorthelp"		"Seamless texture utilizing the red, green and blue channels to create three color masks."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SprayPaint.exposed_params.g_tPattern:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			.important {
			  color: #eaad3d;
			  font-size: 9pt;
			  white-space: pre-wrap;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>How to Create a Pattern</h2>
			<p>Color images are typically stored in red, green and blue channels that combine additively to represent a large range of color values. For our patterns, we take advantage of this configuration to store three separate images. The final result is a bit bright, but don’t worry, what it looks like here isn’t how it’ll look on a weapon.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_b.png' /><br>
			<span class=important><b><u>IMPORTANT!</u></b> Copy the opacity of each layer into the RGB channels of a new image. The base coat is not included.</span><br>
			<h2>Pattern Application Method</h2>
			<p>Spray-Paint finishes are applied using triplanar mapping. Think of it as spray painting though a stencil onto the sides, top, bottom, back and front of the weapon. The pattern blends across the surface normals.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/triplanar_map.png' />
			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SprayPaint.exposed_params.g_flPatternTexCoordScale:name_ref"		"Texture Scale"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SprayPaint.exposed_params.g_flPatternTexCoordScale:shorthelp"		"Controls size of the texture when applied to a weapon. Increasing the scale repeats the pattern."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SprayPaint.exposed_params.g_flPatternTexCoordScale:help"		"			<html>

			<body>
			<p>Controls size of the texture when applied to a weapon. Increasing the scale repeats the pattern.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_a.png' />
			<p>Since the weapons are all different sizes, a paint on a large weapon will have correspondingly large features and a paint on a small weapon will have very tiny features. We fix this by further modifying the scale per-weapon. For most styles the scale of the pattern is relative to a pattern sheet size of 36 inches. For styles that use triplanar mapping, 18 inches.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_b.png' />
			<p>Enable \"Ignore Weapon Size Scale\" when the automatic scale adjustment per-weapon is not desired</p>
			</body>
			</html>"

			<body>
			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Experiment with color harmonies</h2>
			<p>The same pattern can be reused with different colors to create a new finish.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_c.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"

			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Experiment with color harmonies</h2>
			<p>The same pattern can be reused with different colors to create a new finish.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_c.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"

			<p>A greyscale texture that defines the microfacet roughness of the surface. Black is perfectly smooth and white is perfectly rough. The roughness map allows you to define the condition and character of a surface. This can be used to make your finish look distressed and weathered or like it has a fresh coat of paint.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/roughness.png' />
			<p>You can also use a <a href='helpsystem:Attribute.PaintKit_Anodized.exposed_params.g_tNormal'>Normal map</a> to derive surface details that should be represented in the roughness map.</p>
			</body>
			</html>"

			<p>A normal map can give the weapon finish an appearance of depth or bumps without adding more polygons through the use of lighting. Using a normal map can add subtle details to a finish like wood grain or they can be used to create more pronounced changes.</p>

			<body>
			<p>All finishable weapons are divided into regions that define how the finish styles apply their colors and patterns. Paint by number masks control which areas can be anodized or given a patina, and where patterns and accent colors appear.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/paintbynumber.png' />
			<br>
			<p>There are also predefined areas on each weapon that don’t get refinished, such as shell casings, the inside of barrels, firing rods, etc.
			<br><br>
			The best way to visualize the paint by number areas on a weapon is to load it up in the Counter-Strike 2 Workshop Item Editor and assign some colors.</p>

			<body>			
			<h2>How to Create a Pattern</h2>
			<p>Color images are typically stored in red, green and blue channels that combine additively to represent a large range of color values. For our patterns, we take advantage of this configuration to store three separate images. The final result is a bit bright, but don’t worry, what it looks like here isn’t how it’ll look on a weapon.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_b.png' /><br>
			<span class=important><b><u>IMPORTANT!</u></b> Copy the opacity of each layer into the RGB channels of a new image. The base coat is not included.</span><br>
			<h2>Pattern Application Method</h2>
			<p>Anodized Multicolor finishes are applied using triplanar mapping. Think of it as spray painting though a stencil onto the sides, top, bottom, back and front of the weapon. The pattern blends across the surface normals.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/triplanar_map.png' />
			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"

			<p>Controls size of the texture when applied to a weapon. Increasing the scale repeats the pattern.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_a.png' />
			<p>Since the weapons are all different sizes, a paint on a large weapon will have correspondingly large features and a paint on a small weapon will have very tiny features. We fix this by further modifying the scale per-weapon. For most styles the scale of the pattern is relative to a pattern sheet size of 36 inches. For styles that use triplanar mapping, 18 inches.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_b.png' />
			<p>Enable \"Ignore Weapon Size Scale\" when the automatic scale adjustment per-weapon is not desired</p>
			</body>

			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Experiment with color harmonies</h2>
			<p>The same pattern can be reused with different colors to create a new finish.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_c.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"

			<p>All finishable weapons are divided into regions that define how the finish styles apply their colors and patterns. Paint by number masks control which areas can be anodized or given a patina, and where patterns and accent colors appear.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/paintbynumber.png' />
			<br>
			<p>There are also predefined areas on each weapon that don’t get refinished, such as shell casings, the inside of barrels, firing rods, etc.
			<br><br>
			The best way to visualize the paint by number areas on a weapon is to load it up in the Counter-Strike 2 Workshop Item Editor and assign some colors.</p>

			<body>
			<p>In general, finishes should be available in all wear values from Factory New to Battle Scarred with a few exceptions. That said the wear values don't have to be the full range and many weapon finishes ship with wear values from Factory New (0.0) to Battle Scarred (0.6).</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/wear.png' />
			<center>On application, random values are chosen within this range so that each application is unique.</center>
			<br>
			<h3>Wear Value Ranges</h3>
			<ul type=circle>
			<li>Factory New:	0.00 - 0.07</li>
			<li>Minimal Wear:	0.07 - 0.15</li>
			<li>Field Tested:	0.15 - 0.37</li>
			<li>Well Worn:		0.37 - 0.44</li>
			<li>Battle Scarred:	0.44 - 1.0</li>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_AnodizedAirbrushed.exposed_params.g_tPattern:name_ref"		"Pattern Mask"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_AnodizedAirbrushed.exposed_params.g_tPattern:shorthelp"		"Seamless texture utilizing the red, green and blue channels to create three color masks."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_AnodizedAirbrushed.exposed_params.g_tPattern:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			.important {
			  color: #eaad3d;
			  font-size: 9pt;
			  white-space: pre-wrap;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>			
			<h2>How to Create a Pattern</h2>
			<p>Color images are typically stored in red, green and blue channels that combine additively to represent a large range of color values. For our patterns, we take advantage of this configuration to store three separate images. The final result is a bit bright, but don’t worry, what it looks like here isn’t how it’ll look on a weapon.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_b.png' /><br>
			<span class=important><b><u>IMPORTANT!</u></b> Copy the opacity of each layer into the RGB channels of a new image. The base coat is not included.</span><br>
			<h2>Pattern Application Method</h2>
			<p>Anodized Airbrushed finishes are applied using triplanar mapping. Think of it as spray painting though a stencil onto the sides, top, bottom, back and front of the weapon. The pattern blends across the surface normals.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/triplanar_map.png' />
			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_AnodizedAirbrushed.exposed_params.g_flPatternTexCoordScale:name_ref"		"Texture Scale"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_AnodizedAirbrushed.exposed_params.g_flPatternTexCoordScale:shorthelp"		"Controls size of the texture when applied to a weapon. Increasing the scale repeats the pattern."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_AnodizedAirbrushed.exposed_params.g_flPatternTexCoordScale:help"		"			<html>

			</head>
			<body>
			<p>Controls size of the texture when applied to a weapon. Increasing the scale repeats the pattern.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_a.png' />
			<p>Since the weapons are all different sizes, a paint on a large weapon will have correspondingly large features and a paint on a small weapon will have very tiny features. We fix this by further modifying the scale per-weapon. For most styles the scale of the pattern is relative to a pattern sheet size of 36 inches. For styles that use triplanar mapping, 18 inches.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_b.png' />
			<p>Enable \"Ignore Weapon Size Scale\" when the automatic scale adjustment per-weapon is not desired</p>
			</body>
			</html>"

			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Experiment with color harmonies</h2>
			<p>The same pattern can be reused with different colors to create a new finish.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_c.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"

		"Attribute.PaintKit_CustomPaintJob.exposed_params.g_tPattern:name_ref"		"Albedo Texture"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_CustomPaintJob.exposed_params.g_tPattern:shorthelp"		"Full-color image texture. Supports optional alpha channel for paint masking and durability."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_CustomPaintJob.exposed_params.g_tPattern:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			b {
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			.important {
			  color: #eaad3d;
			  font-size: 9pt;
			  white-space: pre-wrap;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Texture Application Method</h2>
			<p>Custom Paint Job finishes simply tile the full-color texture over the weapon’s existing UVs. To relate that to a real-world application, imagine disassembling the weapon into parts before applying the finish.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/uv_map.png' />
						
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<h2>Paint Masking and Durability:</h2>
			<p>On top of their RGB channels, Color textures have an additional, optional “alpha” channel. Custom Paint Job finishes allow paint masking and durability to be specified in the alpha channel.</p>
			<ul>
			<li>Values around 196 in the alpha channel subtract from the refinishable areas of the weapon.</li>
			<li>Both 128 and 255 have no effect, so the finish wears using the default behavior in these areas.</li>
			<li>Values below 128 increase the durability of the finish. The darker the value, the more durable the paint.</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/durability_cu.png' /><br>
			<p>Each finishable weapon uses a special texture to determine what parts should receive finish. This texture also influences how quickly the finish wears off different features of the weapon. The original, unfinished material underneath is called the substrate.</p>
			<br><br>
			<em>
			<u>When to use a pattern’s alpha channel:</u>
			<ul>
			<li>Your design requires more coverage than the default</li>
			<li>Your design requires more of the substrate to be revealed</li>
			<li>Important features of your design wear too quickly</li>
			<li>Important features of your design should never wear to the substrate</li>
			</em>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"

			<p>Since the weapons are all different sizes, a paint on a large weapon will have correspondingly large features and a paint on a small weapon will have very tiny features. We fix this by further modifying the scale per-weapon. For most styles the scale of the pattern is relative to a pattern sheet size of 36 inches. For styles that use triplanar mapping, 18 inches.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_b.png' />

			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			</body>

		"Attribute.PaintKit_Gunsmith.exposed_params.g_tPattern:name_ref"		"Albedo Texture"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_Gunsmith.exposed_params.g_tPattern:shorthelp"		"Full-color image texture. Supports optional alpha channel for paint masking and durability."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_Gunsmith.exposed_params.g_tPattern:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			b {
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			.important {
			  color: #eaad3d;
			  font-size: 9pt;
			  white-space: pre-wrap;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Texture Application Method</h2>
			<p>Gunsmith finishes simply tile the full-color texture over the weapon’s existing UVs. To relate that to a real-world application, imagine disassembling the weapon into parts before applying the finish.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/uv_map.png' />
			
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<h2>Paint Masking and Durability:</h2>
			<p>On top of their RGB channels, Color textures have an additional, optional “alpha” channel. Gunsmith finishes combine Patina and Custom Paint Job styles allowing paint masking and durability to be specified in the alpha channel differently depending on material type.</p>
			<br>
			<p>Areas of the weapon that are painted using the Custom Paint Job style allows paint masking and durability using the alpha channel in those areas.</p>
			<ul>
			<li>Values around 196 in the alpha channel subtract from the refinishable areas of the weapon.</li>
			<li>Both 128 and 255 have no effect, so the finish wears using the default behavior in these areas.</li>
			<li>Values below 128 increase the durability of the finish. The darker the value, the more durable the paint.</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/durability_gs.png' /><br>
			<p>Each finishable weapon uses a special texture to determine what parts should receive finish. This texture also influences how quickly the finish wears off different features of the weapon. The original, unfinished material underneath is called the substrate.</p>
			<br><br>
			<em>
			<u>When to use a pattern’s alpha channel:</u>
			<ul>
			<li>Your design requires more coverage than the default</li>
			<li>Your design requires more of the substrate to be revealed</li>
			<li>Important features of your design wear too quickly</li>
			<li>Important features of your design should never wear to the substrate</li>
			</em>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"

		"Attribute.PaintKit_CaseHardening.exposed_params.g_tPattern:name_ref"		"Albedo Texture"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_CaseHardening.exposed_params.g_tPattern:shorthelp"		"Full-color image texture. Supports optional alpha channel for paint masking and durability."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_CaseHardening.exposed_params.g_tPattern:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			b {
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			.important {
			  color: #eaad3d;
			  font-size: 9pt;
			  white-space: pre-wrap;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Texture Application Method</h2>
			<p>Custom Paint Job finishes simply tile the full-color texture over the weapon’s existing UVs. To relate that to a real-world application, imagine disassembling the weapon into parts before applying the finish.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/uv_map.png' />
						
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<h2>Paint Masking and Durability:</h2>
			<p>On top of their RGB channels, Color textures have an additional, optional “alpha” channel. Custom Paint Job finishes allow paint masking and durability to be specified in the alpha channel.</p>
			<ul>
			<li>Values around 196 in the alpha channel subtract from the refinishable areas of the weapon.</li>
			<li>Both 128 and 255 have no effect, so the finish wears using the default behavior in these areas.</li>
			<li>Values below 128 increase the durability of the finish. The darker the value, the more durable the paint.</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/durability_cu.png' /><br>
			<p>Each finishable weapon uses a special texture to determine what parts should receive finish. This texture also influences how quickly the finish wears off different features of the weapon. The original, unfinished material underneath is called the substrate.</p>
			<br><br>
			<em>
			<u>When to use a pattern’s alpha channel:</u>
			<ul>
			<li>Your design requires more coverage than the default</li>
			<li>Your design requires more of the substrate to be revealed</li>
			<li>Important features of your design wear too quickly</li>
			<li>Important features of your design should never wear to the substrate</li>
			</em>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"

			<p>Since the weapons are all different sizes, a paint on a large weapon will have correspondingly large features and a paint on a small weapon will have very tiny features. We fix this by further modifying the scale per-weapon. For most styles the scale of the pattern is relative to a pattern sheet size of 36 inches. For styles that use triplanar mapping, 18 inches.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_b.png' />
			<p>Enable \"Ignore Weapon Size Scale\" when the automatic scale adjustment per-weapon is not desired</p>

			<p>In general, finishes should be available in all wear values from Factory New to Battle Scarred with a few exceptions. That said the wear values don't have to be the full range and many weapon finishes ship with wear values from Factory New (0.0) to Battle Scarred (0.6).</p>

		"Attribute.PaintKit_CustomPaintJobExtended.exposed_params.g_tPattern:name_ref"		"Albedo Texture"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_CustomPaintJobExtended.exposed_params.g_tPattern:shorthelp"		"Full-color image texture. Supports optional alpha channel for paint masking and durability."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_CustomPaintJobExtended.exposed_params.g_tPattern:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			b {
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			.important {
			  color: #eaad3d;
			  font-size: 9pt;
			  white-space: pre-wrap;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Texture Application Method</h2>
			<p>Custom Paint Job finishes simply tile the full-color texture over the weapon’s existing UVs. To relate that to a real-world application, imagine disassembling the weapon into parts before applying the finish.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/uv_map.png' />
						
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<h2>Paint Masking and Durability:</h2>
			<p>On top of their RGB channels, Color textures have an additional, optional “alpha” channel. Custom Paint Job finishes allow paint masking and durability to be specified in the alpha channel.</p>
			<ul>
			<li>Values around 196 in the alpha channel subtract from the refinishable areas of the weapon.</li>
			<li>Both 128 and 255 have no effect, so the finish wears using the default behavior in these areas.</li>
			<li>Values below 128 increase the durability of the finish. The darker the value, the more durable the paint.</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/durability_cu.png' /><br>
			<p>Each finishable weapon uses a special texture to determine what parts should receive finish. This texture also influences how quickly the finish wears off different features of the weapon. The original, unfinished material underneath is called the substrate.</p>
			<br><br>
			<em>
			<u>When to use a pattern’s alpha channel:</u>
			<ul>
			<li>Your design requires more coverage than the default</li>
			<li>Your design requires more of the substrate to be revealed</li>
			<li>Important features of your design wear too quickly</li>
			<li>Important features of your design should never wear to the substrate</li>
			</em>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"

			<p>Since the weapons are all different sizes, a paint on a large weapon will have correspondingly large features and a paint on a small weapon will have very tiny features. We fix this by further modifying the scale per-weapon. For most styles the scale of the pattern is relative to a pattern sheet size of 36 inches. For styles that use triplanar mapping, 18 inches.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_b.png' />

			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/wear.png' />
			<center>On application, random values are chosen within this range so that each application is unique.</center>
			<br>
			<h3>Wear Value Ranges</h3>
			<ul type=circle>
			<li>Factory New:	0.00 - 0.07</li>
			<li>Minimal Wear:	0.07 - 0.15</li>
			<li>Field Tested:	0.15 - 0.37</li>
			<li>Well Worn:		0.37 - 0.44</li>
			<li>Battle Scarred:	0.44 - 1.0</li>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_GunsmithCaseHardening.exposed_params.g_tPattern:name_ref"		"Albedo Texture"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_GunsmithCaseHardening.exposed_params.g_tPattern:shorthelp"		"Full-color image texture. Supports optional alpha channel for paint masking and durability."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_GunsmithCaseHardening.exposed_params.g_tPattern:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;

			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Texture Application Method</h2>
			<p>Gunsmith finishes simply tile the full-color texture over the weapon’s existing UVs. To relate that to a real-world application, imagine disassembling the weapon into parts before applying the finish.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/uv_map.png' />
			
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<h2>Paint Masking and Durability:</h2>
			<p>On top of their RGB channels, Color textures have an additional, optional “alpha” channel. Gunsmith finishes combine Patina and Custom Paint Job styles allowing paint masking and durability to be specified in the alpha channel differently depending on material type.</p>
			<br>
			<p>Areas of the weapon that are painted using the Custom Paint Job style allows paint masking and durability using the alpha channel in those areas.</p>
			<ul>
			<li>Values around 196 in the alpha channel subtract from the refinishable areas of the weapon.</li>
			<li>Both 128 and 255 have no effect, so the finish wears using the default behavior in these areas.</li>
			<li>Values below 128 increase the durability of the finish. The darker the value, the more durable the paint.</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/durability_gs.png' /><br>
			<p>Each finishable weapon uses a special texture to determine what parts should receive finish. This texture also influences how quickly the finish wears off different features of the weapon. The original, unfinished material underneath is called the substrate.</p>
			<br><br>
			<em>
			<u>When to use a pattern’s alpha channel:</u>
			<ul>
			<li>Your design requires more coverage than the default</li>
			<li>Your design requires more of the substrate to be revealed</li>
			<li>Important features of your design wear too quickly</li>
			<li>Important features of your design should never wear to the substrate</li>
			</em>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"

			<p>In general, finishes should be available in all wear values from Factory New to Battle Scarred with a few exceptions. That said the wear values don't have to be the full range and many weapon finishes ship with wear values from Factory New (0.0) to Battle Scarred (0.6).</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/wear.png' />
			<center>On application, random values are chosen within this range so that each application is unique.</center>
			<br>
			<h3>Wear Value Ranges</h3>
			<ul type=circle>
			<li>Factory New:	0.00 - 0.07</li>
			<li>Minimal Wear:	0.07 - 0.15</li>
			<li>Field Tested:	0.15 - 0.37</li>
			<li>Well Worn:		0.37 - 0.44</li>
			<li>Battle Scarred:	0.44 - 1.0</li>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_GunsmithExtended.exposed_params.g_tPattern:name_ref"		"Albedo Texture"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_GunsmithExtended.exposed_params.g_tPattern:shorthelp"		"Full-color image texture. Supports optional alpha channel for paint masking and durability."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_GunsmithExtended.exposed_params.g_tPattern:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			b {
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			.important {
			  color: #eaad3d;
			  font-size: 9pt;
			  white-space: pre-wrap;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Texture Application Method</h2>
			<p>Custom Paint Job finishes simply tile the full-color texture over the weapon’s existing UVs. To relate that to a real-world application, imagine disassembling the weapon into parts before applying the finish.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/uv_map.png' />
						
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<h2>Paint Masking and Durability:</h2>
			<p>On top of their RGB channels, Color textures have an additional, optional “alpha” channel. Custom Paint Job finishes allow paint masking and durability to be specified in the alpha channel.</p>
			<ul>
			<li>Values around 196 in the alpha channel subtract from the refinishable areas of the weapon.</li>
			<li>Both 128 and 255 have no effect, so the finish wears using the default behavior in these areas.</li>
			<li>Values below 128 increase the durability of the finish. The darker the value, the more durable the paint.</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/durability_cu.png' /><br>
			<p>Each finishable weapon uses a special texture to determine what parts should receive finish. This texture also influences how quickly the finish wears off different features of the weapon. The original, unfinished material underneath is called the substrate.</p>
			<br><br>
			<em>
			<u>When to use a pattern’s alpha channel:</u>
			<ul>
			<li>Your design requires more coverage than the default</li>
			<li>Your design requires more of the substrate to be revealed</li>
			<li>Important features of your design wear too quickly</li>
			<li>Important features of your design should never wear to the substrate</li>
			</em>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"

			<body>
			<h2>How to Create a Pattern</h2>
			<p>Color images are typically stored in red, green and blue channels that combine additively to represent a large range of color values. For our patterns, we take advantage of this configuration to store three separate images. The final result is a bit bright, but don’t worry, what it looks like here isn’t how it’ll look on a weapon.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_b.png' /><br>
			<span class=important><b><u>IMPORTANT!</u></b> Copy the opacity of each layer into the RGB channels of a new image. The base coat is not included.</span><br>
			<h2>Pattern Application Method</h2>
			<p>Hydrographic finishes are UV mapped, the pattern tiles over the weapon’s existing UVs. To relate that to a real-world application, imagine disassembling the weapon into parts before applying the finish.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/uv_map.png' />
			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			<h2>Durability and Masking</h2>
			<p>On top of their RGB channels, Color textures have an additional, optional “alpha” channel. Hydrographic finishes allow paint masking and durability to be specified in the alpha channel.</p>
			<ul>
			<li>Values around 196 in the alpha channel subtract from the refinishable areas of the weapon.</li>
			<li>Both 128 and 255 have no effect, so the finish wears using the default behavior in these areas.</li>
			<li>Values below 128 increase the durability of the finish. The darker the value, the more durable the paint.</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/durability_hy.png' /><br>
			<p>Each finishable weapon uses a special texture to determine what parts should receive finish. This texture also influences how quickly the finish wears off different features of the weapon. The original, unfinished material underneath is called the substrate.</p>
			<br><br>
			<em>
			<u>When to use a pattern’s alpha channel:</u>
			<ul>
			<li>Your design requires more coverage than the default</li>
			<li>Your design requires more of the substrate to be revealed</li>
			<li>Important features of your design wear too quickly</li>
			<li>Important features of your design should never wear to the substrate</li>
			</em>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"

			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_a.png' />
			<p>Since the weapons are all different sizes, a paint on a large weapon will have correspondingly large features and a paint on a small weapon will have very tiny features. We fix this by further modifying the scale per-weapon. For most styles the scale of the pattern is relative to a pattern sheet size of 36 inches. For styles that use triplanar mapping, 18 inches.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_b.png' />
			<p>Enable \"Ignore Weapon Size Scale\" when the automatic scale adjustment per-weapon is not desired</p>
			</body>

			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Experiment with color harmonies</h2>
			<p>The same pattern can be reused with different colors to create a new finish.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_c.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"

		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColorCaseHardening.exposed_params.g_tPattern:name_ref"		"Albedo Texture"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColorCaseHardening.exposed_params.g_tPattern:shorthelp"		"Full-color image texture. Supports optional alpha channel for paint masking and durability."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColorCaseHardening.exposed_params.g_tPattern:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {

			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Texture Application Method</h2>
			<p>Custom Paint Job finishes simply tile the full-color texture over the weapon’s existing UVs. To relate that to a real-world application, imagine disassembling the weapon into parts before applying the finish.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/uv_map.png' />
						
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<h2>Paint Masking and Durability:</h2>
			<p>On top of their RGB channels, Color textures have an additional, optional “alpha” channel. Custom Paint Job finishes allow paint masking and durability to be specified in the alpha channel.</p>
			<ul>
			<li>Values around 196 in the alpha channel subtract from the refinishable areas of the weapon.</li>
			<li>Both 128 and 255 have no effect, so the finish wears using the default behavior in these areas.</li>
			<li>Values below 128 increase the durability of the finish. The darker the value, the more durable the paint.</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/durability_cu.png' /><br>
			<p>Each finishable weapon uses a special texture to determine what parts should receive finish. This texture also influences how quickly the finish wears off different features of the weapon. The original, unfinished material underneath is called the substrate.</p>
			<br><br>
			<em>
			<u>When to use a pattern’s alpha channel:</u>
			<ul>
			<li>Your design requires more coverage than the default</li>
			<li>Your design requires more of the substrate to be revealed</li>
			<li>Important features of your design wear too quickly</li>
			<li>Important features of your design should never wear to the substrate</li>
			</em>
			</ul>
			</body>
			</html>"

		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColorCaseHardening.exposed_params.g_vColor0:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			b {
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			</body>
			</html>"

			<body>
			<p>A greyscale texture that defines the microfacet roughness of the surface. Black is perfectly smooth and white is perfectly rough. The roughness map allows you to define the condition and character of a surface. This can be used to make your finish look distressed and weathered or like it has a fresh coat of paint.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/roughness.png' />
			<p>You can also use a <a href='helpsystem:Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColorCaseHardening.exposed_params.g_tNormal'>Normal map</a> to derive surface details that should be represented in the roughness map.</p>

			  text-indent: 10px;

			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<p>All finishable weapons are divided into regions that define how the finish styles apply their colors and patterns. Paint by number masks control which areas can be anodized or given a patina, and where patterns and accent colors appear.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/paintbynumber.png' />
			<br>
			<p>There are also predefined areas on each weapon that don’t get refinished, such as shell casings, the inside of barrels, firing rods, etc.
			<br><br>
			The best way to visualize the paint by number areas on a weapon is to load it up in the Counter-Strike 2 Workshop Item Editor and assign some colors.</p>
			</body>

			<body>
			<p>In general, finishes should be available in all wear values from Factory New to Battle Scarred with a few exceptions. That said the wear values don't have to be the full range and many weapon finishes ship with wear values from Factory New (0.0) to Battle Scarred (0.6).</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/wear.png' />
			<center>On application, random values are chosen within this range so that each application is unique.</center>
			<br>
			<h3>Wear Value Ranges</h3>
			<ul type=circle>
			<li>Factory New:	0.00 - 0.07</li>
			<li>Minimal Wear:	0.07 - 0.15</li>
			<li>Field Tested:	0.15 - 0.37</li>
			<li>Well Worn:		0.37 - 0.44</li>
			<li>Battle Scarred:	0.44 - 1.0</li>
			</ul>
			</body>

		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColorExtended.exposed_params.g_vColor0:name_ref"		"Base Coat"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColorExtended.exposed_params.g_vColor0:shorthelp"		"A base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SolidColorExtended.exposed_params.g_vColor0:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			b {
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			</body>
			</html>"

		"Attribute.PaintKit_SprayPaintExtended.exposed_params.g_tPattern:name_ref"		"Pattern Mask"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SprayPaintExtended.exposed_params.g_tPattern:shorthelp"		"Seamless texture utilizing the red, green and blue channels to create three color masks."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SprayPaintExtended.exposed_params.g_tPattern:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {

			  white-space: pre-wrap;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>How to Create a Pattern</h2>
			<p>Color images are typically stored in red, green and blue channels that combine additively to represent a large range of color values. For our patterns, we take advantage of this configuration to store three separate images. The final result is a bit bright, but don’t worry, what it looks like here isn’t how it’ll look on a weapon.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_b.png' /><br>
			<span class=important><b><u>IMPORTANT!</u></b> Copy the opacity of each layer into the RGB channels of a new image. The base coat is not included.</span><br>
			<h2>Pattern Application Method</h2>
			<p>Spray-Paint finishes are applied using triplanar mapping. Think of it as spray painting though a stencil onto the sides, top, bottom, back and front of the weapon. The pattern blends across the surface normals.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/triplanar_map.png' />
			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"

			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Experiment with color harmonies</h2>
			<p>The same pattern can be reused with different colors to create a new finish.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_c.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"
