		"Attribute.PaintKit_SprayPaintHalftone.exposed_params.g_tPattern:name_ref"		"Pattern Mask"
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SprayPaintHalftone.exposed_params.g_tPattern:shorthelp"		"Seamless texture utilizing the red, green and blue channels to create three color masks."
		"Attribute.PaintKit_SprayPaintHalftone.exposed_params.g_tPattern:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			.important {
			  color: #eaad3d;
			  font-size: 9pt;
			  white-space: pre-wrap;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>How to Create a Pattern</h2>
			<p>Color images are typically stored in red, green and blue channels that combine additively to represent a large range of color values. For our patterns, we take advantage of this configuration to store three separate images. The final result is a bit bright, but don’t worry, what it looks like here isn’t how it’ll look on a weapon.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_b.png' /><br>
			<span class=important><b><u>IMPORTANT!</u></b> Copy the opacity of each layer into the RGB channels of a new image. The base coat is not included.</span><br>
			<h2>Pattern Application Method</h2>
			<p>Spray-Paint finishes are applied using triplanar mapping. Think of it as spray painting though a stencil onto the sides, top, bottom, back and front of the weapon. The pattern blends across the surface normals.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/triplanar_map.png' />
			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"

			<body>
			<p>Controls size of the texture when applied to a weapon. Increasing the scale repeats the pattern.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_a.png' />
			<p>Since the weapons are all different sizes, a paint on a large weapon will have correspondingly large features and a paint on a small weapon will have very tiny features. We fix this by further modifying the scale per-weapon. For most styles the scale of the pattern is relative to a pattern sheet size of 36 inches. For styles that use triplanar mapping, 18 inches.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/pattern_scale_b.png' />
			<p>Enable \"Ignore Weapon Size Scale\" when the automatic scale adjustment per-weapon is not desired</p>
			</body>
			</html>"

			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Experiment with color harmonies</h2>
			<p>The same pattern can be reused with different colors to create a new finish.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_c.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"

			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			b {
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Color Application Process</h2>
			<p>The pattern is applied one layer at a time, starting with a base coat that covers all paintable areas of the weapon followed by the red, green, and blue channels in that order.</p>
			<br><br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_a.png' />
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires weapon finishes to be authored within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_a.png' />
			<p>For metallic finishes like Anodized Multicolored, Patina, and the metallic portions of Gunsmith, the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/color_b.png' />
			<p>For non-metallic finishes, the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Finishes using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your albedo texture is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/weapon_pbr.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<br>
			<h2>Experiment with color harmonies</h2>
			<p>The same pattern can be reused with different colors to create a new finish.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/patterns_c.png' />
			</body>
			</html>"

			<body>
			<p>All finishable weapons are divided into regions that define how the finish styles apply their colors and patterns. Paint by number masks control which areas can be anodized or given a patina, and where patterns and accent colors appear.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/paintbynumber.png' />
			<br>
			<p>There are also predefined areas on each weapon that don’t get refinished, such as shell casings, the inside of barrels, firing rods, etc.
			<br><br>
			The best way to visualize the paint by number areas on a weapon is to load it up in the Counter-Strike 2 Workshop Item Editor and assign some colors.</p>
			</body>

		"Attribute.StickerKit_Holographic.exposed_param.TextureHoloMaskSticker0:name_ref"		"Holo Mask"
		"Attribute.StickerKit_Holographic.exposed_param.TextureHoloMaskSticker0:shorthelp"		"Texture utilizing the red, green and blue channels to output three color masks used to create the holographic effect."
		"Attribute.StickerKit_Holographic.exposed_param.TextureHoloMaskSticker0:help"		"Uses the textures RGB channels to transport 3 different masks to the game.<br>
			<br>
			<b>Red Channel -</b> masks the areas of the sticker to have the holographic effect applied (white). Areas that have no holographic effect (black) will show the stickers albedo texture as if it were a regular paper backed sticker.<br>
			<br>
			<b>Green Channel -</b> defines where the warp effect will start on the horizontal axis of the Holo Spectrum texture. It will move along this axis depending on the angle of the lighting in game  (see the animated example)<br>
			<br>
			<b>Blue Channel -</b> defines the vertical offset sampling on the Holo Mask texture. This is unaffected by the lighting and allows higher levels of customization of the holographic effect (in the example, you can see that it uses two different color blends from different parts of the spectrum)"
		"Attribute.StickerKit_Holographic.exposed_param.TextureWearMaskSticker0:name_ref"		"Wear Mask"
		"Attribute.StickerKit_Holographic.exposed_param.TextureWearMaskSticker0:help"		"A greyscale mask that allows you to control the rate of decay of a sticker when its scratched eg. allowing you to preserve important areas you want to be visible for longer.<br>
			<br>
			Painting in grey values of greater than 30 (out of 255) in this image will slow the wear."
		"Attribute.StickerKit_Holographic.exposed_param.TextureHoloSpectrumSticker0:name_ref"		"Holo Spectrum"
		"Attribute.StickerKit_Holographic.exposed_param.TextureHoloSpectrumSticker0:help"		"Full-color image texture that defines the color shown on the texture where the holomask is visible. It will transition across this texture horizontally as the angle of the light changes."

		"Attribute.StickerKit_Holographic.exposed_param.g_bAutomaticPBRColorFittingSticker0:help"		"			<html>
			<head>
			<style>
			body {
			  font-family: Stratum2 Condensed;
			  font-size: 10pt;
			}
			h2 {
			  text-transform: uppercase;
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			b {
			  color: #54bff4;
			}
			p {
			  text-indent: 10px;
			}
			</style>
			</head>
			<body>
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering ( PBR )</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires stickers to be within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/sticker_color.png' />
			<p>For foil stickers the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<p>For Paper, Holographic, and Glitter stickers the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Stickers using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your sticker is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/sticker_pbr_autofit.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<br>
			</body>
			</html>"

			<body>
			<p>Controls the wear intensity of the top color layer independent from the paper backing. The example images below were both captured at a wear level of 0.50 and by lowering the \"Wear Bias Color\" we can preserve more of the color at the same wear level.</p>

			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/sticker_wear_bias_color.png' /><br>

			<body>
			<h2>Physically Based Rendering ( PBR )</h2>
			<p>CS2 uses physically based rendering which requires stickers to be within the effective PBR range for that material.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/sticker_color.png' />
			<p>For foil stickers the effective RGB range is most likely between <b>180-250</b>. Values as low as <b>90</b> may be acceptable depending on the color's saturation.</p>
			<p>For Paper, Holographic, and Glitter stickers the effective reflectance range is between <b>55-220</b>. Albedo values outside of this range will not respond appropriately to in-game lighting conditions. Stickers using values outside the effective PBR range are unlikely to be selected from the workshop.</p>
			<h2>Checking Texture PBR</h2>
			<p>To check if your sticker is PBR safe open VConsole2(~) and enter \"mat_fullbright 10\" to enter Albedo mode highlighting any colors outside of PBR range.</p>
			<br>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/sticker_pbr_autofit.png' />
			<ul>
			<li><b style=\"color: #949bfe\">Blue</b> - Below the PBR threshold appearing too dark</li>
			<li><b style=\"color: #fe9494\">Red</b> - Above the PBR threshold appearing too bright</li>
			</ul>
			<br>
			<br>
			<p>You can also access this by clicking the ConVar button in VConsole2 to open the ConVar Helper. In the \"csgo art\" page you can click the \"Albedo\" button to toggle \"mat_fullbright 10\"</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/albedo_toggle.png' />
			<br>
			<br>
			</body>
			</html>"

			<h2>Solid Color Style:</h2>

			<p>The weapon is spray-painted with multiple coats through stencil patterns.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/comp_spray.png' />

			<h2>Hydrographic Style</h2>
			<p>Disassembled weapon parts are lowered through a floating hydrographic film on the surface of a water tank. The film adheres to the primed weapon parts, covering the surface with a pattern.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/comp_hydrographic.png' />

			<h2>Anodized Style</h2>
			<p>Many common firearms materials cannot be anodized. Instead the effect is often mimicked by applying a colored candy coat over a chrome base.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/comp_anodized.png' />

			<h2>Anodized Multicolored Style</h2>
			<p>In this style, the candy coat may be applied in a multicolored pattern. In the real world, methods could include silk-screening or adherable stencils.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/comp_anodized_multi.png' />

			<h2>Anodized Airbrushed Style</h2>
			<p>This style emulates applying the candy coat via freehand airbrushing.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/comp_anodized_airbrush.png' />

			<h2>Patina Style</h2>
			<p>A patina is a chemical reaction that forms a non-reactive, hardened shell over metallic parts. Real-life weapon patinas include case hardening, cold bluing, and acid forced patinas.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/comp_patina.png' />

			<h2>Custom Paint Style</h2>
			<p>This style enables extremely customized looks in a full range of colors.</p>
			<br>
			<img src='game:tools/cs2_item_editor/comp_custom.png' />
